    19â†’MRPP tests the hypothesis that there is no difference between two or more groups
    20â†’of entities. It is a non-parametric procedure that uses only the distance matrix
    21â†’without assumptions about underlying distributions.
    22â†’
    23â†’**Key Statistics:**
    24â†’
    25â†’- **delta (Î´)**: Weighted mean of within-group distances
    26â†’  - Lower values indicate more homogeneous groups
    27â†’
    28â†’- **Expected delta (E[Î´])**: Expected value under null hypothesis of random grouping
    29â†’
    30â†’- **A statistic**: Chance-corrected within-group agreement
    31â†’  - A = 1 - (observed_delta / expected_delta)
    32â†’  - A = 1: All samples within groups are identical
    33â†’  - A = 0: Heterogeneity equals expectation by chance
    34â†’  - A < 0: More heterogeneous than expected (unusual)
    35â†’  - A > 0.3: Fairly strong group separation (ecological rule of thumb)
    36â†’
    37â†’**Comparison with Other Tests:**
    38â†’- MRPP: Uses within-group distances only, weighted by group size
    39â†’- ANOSIM: Uses ranks of distances, compares within vs between
    40â†’- PERMANOVA: Uses sums of squares, tests centroid differences
    41â†’
    42â†’MRPP is often preferred when group sizes are unequal because the weighting

    16â†’description = "Distance-based Redundancy Analysis - constrained ordination relating community composition to environmental variables"
    17â†’
    18â†’long_description = """
    19â†’db-RDA (distance-based Redundancy Analysis) is a constrained ordination method that
    20â†’relates community composition (via a distance matrix) to environmental or experimental
    21â†’variables. It extends PCoA by incorporating predictor variables.
    22â†’
    23â†’**How it works:**
    24â†’
    25â†’1. Compute PCoA on the distance matrix to get sample coordinates
    26â†’2. Perform RDA using PCoA axes as response variables and metadata as predictors
    27â†’3. Partition variance into constrained (explained by predictors) and unconstrained components
    28â†’
    29â†’**Key Outputs:**
    30â†’
    31â†’- **Constrained axes**: Ordination axes that represent variation explained by predictors
    32â†’- **Unconstrained axes**: Residual variation not explained by predictors (like PCA on residuals)
    33â†’- **RÂ²**: Proportion of total variation explained by predictors
    34â†’- **Adjusted RÂ²**: RÂ² corrected for number of predictors
    35â†’- **Pseudo-F**: Test statistic for overall significance (via permutation test)
    36â†’
    37â†’**Use Cases:**
    38â†’- Test if environmental variables explain community composition
    39â†’- Visualize how communities relate to measured predictors
    40â†’- Quantify variance explained by experimental design
    41â†’- Partition variance among different sets of predictors (variation partitioning)
    42â†’
    43â†’**Comparison with Other Methods:**
    44â†’- PCoA: Unconstrained ordination (no predictors)
    45â†’- RDA: Constrained ordination on raw data (Euclidean distance only)
    46â†’- CCA: Constrained correspondence analysis (Chi-square distance, unimodal response)
    47â†’- db-RDA: Constrained ordination on any distance metric
    48â†’"""
    49â†’

   123â†’
   124â†’1. PCoA transformation of distance matrix:
   125â†’   - Compute PCoA on distance matrix D to get coordinates Y
   126â†’   - Y is an (n Ã— m) matrix where m = min(n-1, p) positive eigenvalue axes
   127â†’
   128â†’2. RDA on PCoA coordinates:
   129â†’   - X = design matrix from metadata predictors
   130â†’   - B = (X'X)^(-1) X'Y = regression coefficients
   131â†’   - Å¶ = XB = fitted values (constrained scores)
   132â†’   - E = Y - Å¶ = residuals (unconstrained scores)
   133â†’
   134â†’3. Eigendecomposition:

   136â†’   - Unconstrained: eigendecompose E'E for residual axes
   137â†’

   140â†’   - Constrained SS = trace(Å¶'Å¶)
   141â†’   - Unconstrained SS = trace(E'E)
   142â†’   - RÂ² = Constrained SS / Total SS
   143â†’

   145â†’   - Pseudo-F = (Constrained SS / df_constrained) / (Unconstrained SS / df_residual)
   146â†’   - Permute rows of Y, recompute F
   147â†’   - p-value = (count of F_perm â‰¥ F_obs + 1) / (n_perm + 1)
   148â†’"""
   149â†’

   151â†’
   152â†’notes = """
   153â†’Implementation notes:
   154â†’1. Handle negative eigenvalues from PCoA (Lingoes or Cailliez correction, or sqrt transformation)
   155â†’2. For categorical predictors, use dummy coding (n-1 columns for n levels)
   156â†’3. Interaction terms expand the design matrix
   157â†’4. Center Y and X matrices before regression

     1â†’# =============================================================================
     2â†’# Primitive Specification: simper
     3â†’# =============================================================================
     4â†’# SIMPER (Similarity Percentages) breaks down the contribution of each feature
     5â†’# to the Bray-Curtis dissimilarity between groups.
     6â†’#
     7â†’# Reference: Clarke, K.R. (1993). Non-parametric multivariate analyses of changes
     8â†’# in community structure. Australian Journal of Ecology, 18, 117-143.
     9â†’#
    10â†’# R package: vegan, function: simper()
    11â†’# =============================================================================
    12â†’
    13â†’[primitive]
    14â†’name = "simper"
    15â†’category = "test"
    16â†’description = "Similarity percentage breakdown - identifies features driving group differences"
    17â†’
    18â†’long_description = """
    19â†’SIMPER (SIMilarity PERcentages) decomposes Bray-Curtis dissimilarity between groups
    20â†’to identify which features contribute most to the observed differences.
    21â†’
    22â†’**Key Statistics:**
    23â†’
    24â†’- **Average contribution**: Mean contribution of each feature to between-group dissimilarity
    25â†’- **SD**: Standard deviation of contribution (consistency across sample pairs)
    26â†’- **Ratio**: Average/SD - higher values indicate more consistent contributors
    27â†’- **Cumulative %**: Running sum of contributions (features ordered by contribution)
    28â†’
    29â†’**Use Cases:**
    30â†’- After significant PERMANOVA/ANOSIM, identify which species/features drive the difference
    31â†’- Rank features by their discriminatory power between groups
    32â†’- Cumulative contribution helps identify minimum set of distinguishing features
    33â†’
    34â†’**Interpretation:**
    35â†’- Features with high average contribution AND high ratio are reliable discriminators
    36â†’- High contribution but low ratio = inconsistent (varies across sample pairs)
    37â†’- First few features often explain majority of dissimilarity
    38â†’
    39â†’**Limitations:**
    40â†’- Only works with Bray-Curtis dissimilarity
    41â†’- Computationally intensive for large datasets (all pairwise comparisons)
    42â†’- Does not test significance (use with PERMANOVA/ANOSIM for inference)
    43â†’"""
    44â†’
    45â†’# =============================================================================
    46â†’# Parameters
    47â†’# =============================================================================
    48â†’
    49â†’[params.grouping_column]
    50â†’type = "string"
    51â†’required = true
    52â†’description = "Name of the metadata column containing group assignments"
    53â†’
    54â†’[params.group1]
    55â†’type = "string"
    56â†’required = false
    57â†’description = "First group to compare (if not specified, compares all pairs)"
    58â†’
    59â†’[params.group2]

    68â†’default = 20

    70â†’

    73â†’required = false

    75â†’max = 1.0

    78â†’
    79â†’# =============================================================================

    83â†’[[inputs]]
    84â†’slot = "counts"
    85â†’required = true
    86â†’description = "Count/abundance matrix (features Ã— samples)"
    87â†’
    88â†’[[inputs]]
    89â†’slot = "metadata"
    90â†’required = true

    92â†’
    93â†’# =============================================================================
    94â†’# Outputs

    96â†’
    97â†’[[outputs]]
    98â†’slot = "test_statistics"
    99â†’description = "Feature contributions to between-group dissimilarity"
   100â†’
   101â†’[[outputs]]
   102â†’slot = "characteristics"
   103â†’description = "Summary: overall dissimilarity, top contributors, cumulative stats"
   104â†’
   105â†’# =============================================================================
   106â†’# Algorithm
   107â†’# =============================================================================
   108â†’
   109â†’[algorithm]
   110â†’definition = "bioanvil/definitions/simper.md"
   111â†’
   112â†’formula = """
   113â†’SIMPER Calculation:
   114â†’
   115â†’1. For each pair of samples (i from group A, j from group B):
   116â†’
   117â†’   Bray-Curtis dissimilarity:
   118â†’   BC_ij = Î£_k |x_ik - x_jk| / Î£_k (x_ik + x_jk)
   119â†’
   120â†’   Contribution of feature k to BC_ij:
   121â†’   Î´_ijk = |x_ik - x_jk| / Î£_k (x_ik + x_jk)
   122â†’
   123â†’2. For each feature k, average contribution across all between-group pairs:
   124â†’   Î´Ì„_k = mean(Î´_ijk) for all iâˆˆA, jâˆˆB
   125â†’
   126â†’   Standard deviation:
   127â†’   SD_k = sd(Î´_ijk)
   128â†’
   129â†’   Ratio (consistency):
   130â†’   ratio_k = Î´Ì„_k / SD_k
   131â†’
   132â†’3. Overall average dissimilarity:
   133â†’   BCÌ„ = mean(BC_ij) for all iâˆˆA, jâˆˆB
   134â†’
   135â†’4. Percent contribution:
   136â†’   %_k = 100 Ã— Î´Ì„_k / BCÌ„
   137â†’
   138â†’5. Cumulative contribution (ordered by Î´Ì„_k descending):
   139â†’   cumsum_k = Î£_{i=1}^{k} %_i
   140â†’"""
   141â†’
   142â†’complexity = "O(n_A Ã— n_B Ã— n_features)"
   143â†’
   144â†’notes = """
   145â†’Implementation notes:
   146â†’1. Compute relative abundances first (divide each sample by its total)
   147â†’2. For all pairs of samples between groups, compute per-feature contributions
   148â†’3. Average contributions across pairs for each feature
   149â†’4. Sort by contribution, compute cumulative percentages
   150â†’5. Report top_n features or those reaching cumsum_threshold
   151â†’
   152â†’Edge cases:
   153â†’- Features absent in both groups contribute 0
   154â†’- Features with 0 variance (same in all samples) still contribute if different between groups
   155â†’- Very sparse data may have many features with minimal contribution
   156â†’"""
   157â†’

     1â†’# =============================================================================
     2â†’# Primitive Specification: lefse
     3â†’# =============================================================================
     4â†’# LEfSe (Linear discriminant analysis Effect Size) for biomarker discovery.
     5â†’#
     6â†’# Reference: Segata et al. (2011). Metagenomic biomarker discovery and
     7â†’# explanation. Genome Biology, 12, R60.
     8â†’# =============================================================================
     9â†’
    10â†’[primitive]
    11â†’name = "lefse"
    12â†’category = "test"
    13â†’description = "Identify biomarkers using Linear Discriminant Analysis Effect Size (LEfSe)"
    14â†’
    15â†’long_description = """
    16â†’LEfSe (Linear discriminant analysis Effect Size) identifies features that
    17â†’explain differences between groups. The analysis proceeds in three steps:
    18â†’
    19â†’1. **Kruskal-Wallis test**: Non-parametric test to detect features with
    20â†’   significant differential abundance between groups. Only features passing
    21â†’   this test proceed to the next step.
    22â†’
    23â†’2. **Pairwise Wilcoxon tests** (optional): If subclass is specified, tests
    24â†’   biological consistency by ensuring the feature shows the same trend in
    25â†’   all pairwise comparisons within the main class.
    26â†’
    27â†’3. **Linear Discriminant Analysis (LDA)**: Estimates the effect size of each
    28â†’   significant feature. Only features with LDA score above the threshold
    29â†’   are reported as biomarkers.
    30â†’
    31â†’LEfSe is particularly useful for microbiome data as it:
    32â†’- Uses non-parametric statistical tests (robust to non-normality)
    33â†’- Provides effect size estimation (not just p-values)
    34â†’- Handles multi-class comparisons
    35â†’- Optionally checks subclass consistency
    36â†’"""
    37â†’
    38â†’# =============================================================================
    39â†’# Parameters
    40â†’# =============================================================================
    41â†’
    42â†’[params.grouping_column]
    43â†’type = "string"
    44â†’required = true
    45â†’description = "Name of the metadata column containing the main class labels"

    76â†’type = "boolean"

   100â†’description = "Sample metadata containing the grouping variable(s)"
   101â†’
   102â†’# =============================================================================
   103â†’# Outputs

   105â†’
   106â†’[[outputs]]
   107â†’slot = "test_statistics"
   108â†’description = "LDA effect sizes for significant biomarkers"
   109â†’
   110â†’[[outputs]]

   117â†’
   118â†’[[outputs]]
   119â†’slot = "characteristics"
   120â†’description = "Full results: feature_id, group, kw_pvalue, lda_score, is_biomarker"
   121â†’
   122â†’# =============================================================================
   123â†’# Algorithm
   124â†’# =============================================================================
   125â†’
   126â†’[algorithm]
   127â†’method = "LEfSe (Linear discriminant analysis Effect Size)"
   128â†’
   129â†’formula = """
   130â†’Step 1 - Kruskal-Wallis H-test:
   131â†’  H = (12 / (N(N+1))) Ã— Î£(n_i Ã— (RÌ„_i - RÌ„)Â²)
   132â†’
   133â†’  Where:
   134â†’    N = total samples
   135â†’    n_i = samples in group i
   136â†’    RÌ„_i = mean rank in group i
   137â†’    RÌ„ = overall mean rank
   138â†’
   139â†’Step 2 - Pairwise Wilcoxon (if subclass specified):
   140â†’  For each pair of subclasses within different main classes,
   141â†’  test that the difference direction is consistent.
   142â†’
   143â†’Step 3 - LDA effect size:
   144â†’  Features are projected onto the discriminant axis.
   145â†’  Effect size = log10(1 + |Î¼_enriched - Î¼_overall|) Ã— sign
   146â†’
   147â†’  Only features with effect size > lda_threshold are reported.
   148â†’"""
   149â†’
   150â†’complexity = "O(n_features Ã— n_samples Ã— log(n_samples))"

    19â†’
    20â†’- **Specificity (A)**: How concentrated a feature's abundance is within a group
    21â†’  - A = 1: Feature only found in this group

   160â†’  return { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges };
   161â†’}
   162â†’
   163â†’type FilterMode = "all" | "operations" | "recent-5" | "recent-10";
   164â†’
   165â†’interface ProvenanceTabProps {
   166â†’  /** Increment this to trigger a refresh (e.g., when SSE events arrive) */
   167â†’  refreshTrigger?: number;
   168â†’}
   169â†’
   170â†’export function ProvenanceTab({ refreshTrigger = 0 }: ProvenanceTabProps) {
   171â†’  const [graph, setGraph] = useState<ProvenanceGraph | null>(null);
   172â†’  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true);
   173â†’  const [selectedNode, setSelectedNode] = useState<ProvenanceNode | null>(null);
   174â†’  const [nodes, setNodes, onNodesChange] = useNodesState<Node>([]);
   175â†’  const [edges, setEdges, onEdgesChange] = useEdgesState<Edge>([]);
   176â†’  const [filterMode, setFilterMode] = useState<FilterMode>("all");
   177â†’
   178â†’  // Filter graph based on current filter mode
   179â†’  const filterGraph = useCallback((data: ProvenanceGraph, mode: FilterMode): ProvenanceGraph => {
   180â†’    if (mode === "all") return data;
   181â†’
   182â†’    let filteredNodes = [...data.nodes];
   183â†’    let filteredEdges = [...data.edges];
   184â†’
   185â†’    if (mode === "operations") {
   186â†’      // Show only operation nodes and their directly connected artifacts
   187â†’      const operationIds = new Set(data.nodes.filter(n => n.type === "operation").map(n => n.id));
   188â†’      const connectedArtifactIds = new Set<string>();
   189â†’
   190â†’      data.edges.forEach(e => {
   191â†’        if (operationIds.has(e.source)) connectedArtifactIds.add(e.target);
   192â†’        if (operationIds.has(e.target)) connectedArtifactIds.add(e.source);
   193â†’      });
   194â†’
   195â†’      const keepIds = new Set([...Array.from(operationIds), ...Array.from(connectedArtifactIds)]);
   196â†’      filteredNodes = data.nodes.filter(n => keepIds.has(n.id));
   197â†’      filteredEdges = data.edges.filter(e => keepIds.has(e.source) && keepIds.has(e.target));
   198â†’    } else if (mode === "recent-5" || mode === "recent-10") {
   199â†’      // Show only the N most recent operations and their connected artifacts
   200â†’      const limit = mode === "recent-5" ? 5 : 10;
   201â†’      const operations = data.nodes
   202â†’        .filter(n => n.type === "operation" && n.executed_at)
   203â†’        .sort((a, b) => new Date(b.executed_at!).getTime() - new Date(a.executed_at!).getTime())
   204â†’        .slice(0, limit);
   205â†’
   206â†’      const operationIds = new Set(operations.map(n => n.id));
   207â†’      const connectedArtifactIds = new Set<string>();
   208â†’
   209â†’      data.edges.forEach(e => {
   210â†’        if (operationIds.has(e.source)) connectedArtifactIds.add(e.target);
   211â†’        if (operationIds.has(e.target)) connectedArtifactIds.add(e.source);
   212â†’      });
   213â†’
   214â†’      const keepIds = new Set([...Array.from(operationIds), ...Array.from(connectedArtifactIds)]);
   215â†’      filteredNodes = data.nodes.filter(n => keepIds.has(n.id));
   216â†’      filteredEdges = data.edges.filter(e => keepIds.has(e.source) && keepIds.has(e.target));
   217â†’    }
   218â†’
   219â†’    return { ...data, nodes: filteredNodes, edges: filteredEdges };
   220â†’  }, []);
   221â†’
   222â†’  // Apply layout to current graph data with filtering
   223â†’  const applyLayout = useCallback(() => {
   224â†’    if (graph && graph.nodes.length > 0) {
   225â†’      const filtered = filterGraph(graph, filterMode);
   226â†’      const { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges } = layoutGraph(
   227â†’        filtered.nodes,
   228â†’        filtered.edges
   229â†’      );
   230â†’      setNodes(layoutedNodes);
   231â†’      setEdges(layoutedEdges);
   232â†’    }
   233â†’  }, [graph, filterMode, filterGraph, setNodes, setEdges]);
   234â†’
   235â†’  // Load provenance data and apply layout
   236â†’  const loadProvenance = useCallback(async () => {
   237â†’    setLoading(true);
   238â†’    const data = await fetchProvenance();
   239â†’    setGraph(data);
   240â†’
   241â†’    if (data.nodes.length > 0) {
   242â†’      const filtered = filterGraph(data, filterMode);
   243â†’      const { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges } = layoutGraph(
   244â†’        filtered.nodes,
   245â†’        filtered.edges
   246â†’      );
   247â†’      setNodes(layoutedNodes);
   248â†’      setEdges(layoutedEdges);
   249â†’    }
   250â†’
   251â†’    setLoading(false);
   252â†’  }, [filterMode, filterGraph, setNodes, setEdges]);
   253â†’
   254â†’  // Reset layout without refetching data
   255â†’  const resetLayout = useCallback(() => {
   256â†’    applyLayout();
   257â†’  }, [applyLayout]);
   258â†’
   259â†’  // Re-apply layout when filter changes
   260â†’  useEffect(() => {
   261â†’    if (graph) {
   262â†’      applyLayout();
   263â†’    }
   264â†’  }, [filterMode]); // eslint-disable-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps
   265â†’
   266â†’  useEffect(() => {
   267â†’    loadProvenance();
   268â†’  }, [loadProvenance]);
   269â†’
   270â†’  // Auto-refresh when trigger changes (SSE events)
   271â†’  useEffect(() => {
   272â†’    if (refreshTrigger > 0) {
   273â†’      loadProvenance();
   274â†’    }
   275â†’  }, [refreshTrigger]); // eslint-disable-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps
   276â†’
   277â†’  const onNodeClick = useCallback(
   278â†’    (_: React.MouseEvent, node: Node) => {
   279â†’      const provenanceNode = graph?.nodes.find((n) => n.id === node.id);
   280â†’      setSelectedNode(provenanceNode || null);
   281â†’    },
   282â†’    [graph]
   283â†’  );
   284â†’
   285â†’  const stats = graph?.stats;
   286â†’
   287â†’  if (loading && !graph) {
   288â†’    return (
   289â†’      <div className="flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-full gap-4 text-muted-foreground">
   290â†’        <Loader2 className="w-8 h-8 animate-spin" />
   291â†’        <p>Loading provenance graph...</p>
   292â†’      </div>
   293â†’    );
   294â†’  }
   295â†’

   314â†’
   315â†’  return (

    20â†’
    21â†’interface HistoryTabProps {
    22â†’  entries: HistoryEntry[];  // Live SSE entries (for running operations)

    25â†’  refreshTrigger?: number;
    26â†’}
    27â†’
    28â†’export function HistoryTab({ entries: liveEntries, events, refreshTrigger = 0 }: HistoryTabProps) {
    29â†’  const [search, setSearch] = useState("");
    30â†’  const [filterStatus, setFilterStatus] = useState<
    31â†’    "all" | "success" | "error" | "running"

    33â†’  const [copiedId, setCopiedId] = useState<string | null>(null);

    57â†’    }
    58â†’  }, [refreshTrigger, loadOperations]);

    60â†’  // Convert operations to HistoryEntry format

    62â†’    id: op.id,
    63â†’    type: "primitive" as const,
    64â†’    content: op.primitive,
    65â†’    timestamp: new Date(op.executed_at),
    66â†’    status: op.status === "pending" ? "running" : op.status,
    67â†’    duration: op.duration_ms,
    68â†’    outputs: op.outputs,
    69â†’  }));
    70â†’
    71â†’  // Merge live entries (running operations from SSE) with historical operations
    72â†’  // Live entries take precedence for matching IDs
    73â†’  const liveIds = new Set(liveEntries.map((e) => e.id));
    74â†’  const mergedEntries = [
    75â†’    ...liveEntries.filter((e) => e.status === "running"), // Keep running ops from SSE
    76â†’    ...operationEntries.filter((e) => !liveIds.has(e.id)), // Add historical ops not in SSE
    77â†’  ].sort((a, b) => b.timestamp.getTime() - a.timestamp.getTime());
    78â†’
    79â†’  const filteredEntries = mergedEntries.filter((entry) => {
    80â†’    const matchesSearch = entry.content

    82â†’      .includes(search.toLowerCase());
    83â†’    const matchesStatus =
    84â†’      filterStatus === "all" || entry.status === filterStatus;
    85â†’    return matchesSearch && matchesStatus;
    86â†’  });
    87â†’
    88â†’  const handleCopy = async (entry: HistoryEntry) => {
    89â†’    try {
    90â†’      const operation = operations.find((op) => op.id === entry.id);
    91â†’      const content = operation
    92â†’        ? JSON.stringify(

    94â†’              primitive: operation.primitive,
    95â†’              params: operation.params,
    96â†’              inputs: operation.inputs,
    97â†’              outputs: operation.outputs,
    98â†’            },
    99â†’            null,
   100â†’            2
   101â†’          )
   102â†’        : entry.content;
   103â†’      await navigator.clipboard.writeText(content);
   104â†’      setCopiedId(entry.id);
   105â†’      setTimeout(() => setCopiedId(null), 2000);
   106â†’    } catch (err) {
   107â†’      console.error("Failed to copy:", err);
   108â†’    }
   109â†’  };
   110â†’
   111â†’  const getStatusIcon = (status: HistoryEntry["status"]) => {
   112â†’    switch (status) {
   113â†’      case "success":
   114â†’        return <CheckCircle2 className="w-4 h-4 text-success" />;
   115â†’      case "error":
   116â†’        return <XCircle className="w-4 h-4 text-destructive" />;
   117â†’      case "running":
   118â†’        return <Loader2 className="w-4 h-4 text-primary animate-spin" />;
   119â†’    }
   120â†’  };
   121â†’
   122â†’  const getOperation = (id: string): Operation | undefined => {
   123â†’    return operations.find((op) => op.id === id);
   124â†’  };
   125â†’
   126â†’  return (
   127â†’    <div className="flex flex-col h-full">

    68â†’function inferPlotType(data: Record<string, unknown>): PlotInfo["type"] {
    69â†’  const spec = data.vega_lite_spec as Record<string, unknown> | undefined;
    70â†’  if (!spec) return "unknown";
    71â†’
    72â†’  const mark = spec.mark;
    73â†’  if (typeof mark === "string") {
    74â†’    if (mark === "point" || mark === "circle") return "scatter";
    75â†’    if (mark === "bar") return "bar";
    76â†’    if (mark === "rect") return "heatmap";
    77â†’  }
    78â†’  if (typeof mark === "object" && mark !== null) {
    79â†’    const markType = (mark as Record<string, unknown>).type;
    80â†’    if (markType === "point" || markType === "circle") return "scatter";
    81â†’    if (markType === "bar") return "bar";
    82â†’    if (markType === "rect") return "heatmap";
    83â†’  }
    84â†’
    85â†’  return "ordination";
    86â†’}

   118â†’ * @param options.primitive - Filter by primitive name
   119â†’ */
   120â†’export async function fetchOperations(options?: {
   121â†’  limit?: number;
   122â†’  offset?: number;
   123â†’  status?: string;
   124â†’  primitive?: string;

   132â†’
   133â†’    const url = params.toString()
   134â†’      ? `${DAEMON_URL}/operations?${params.toString()}`
   135â†’      : `${DAEMON_URL}/operations`;
   136â†’
   137â†’    const response = await fetch(url);
   138â†’    if (!response.ok) {
   139â†’      console.error("Failed to fetch operations:", response.statusText);

   143â†’  } catch (error) {

   145â†’    return { operations: [], total: 0, limit: 100, offset: 0 };
   146â†’  }
   147â†’}

/**
 * Fetch provenance graph data (nodes and edges for DAG visualization).

export async function fetchProvenance(): Promise<ProvenanceGraph> {
  try {
    const response = await fetch(`${DAEMON_URL}/provenance`);
    if (!response.ok) {
      console.error("Failed to fetch provenance:", response.statusText);
      return { nodes: [], edges: [] };
    }
    return await response.json();
  } catch (error) {
    console.error("Error fetching provenance:", error);
    return { nodes: [], edges: [] };
  }
}

/Users/scotthandley/Code/biostack/bioview-web/components/graphs/VersionDAG.tsx


"use client";

import { useState, useEffect, useCallback, useMemo } from "react";
import {
  ReactFlow,
  Node,
  Edge,
  Controls,
  Background,
  MiniMap,
  useNodesState,
  useEdgesState,
  MarkerType,
  Position,
  Handle,
} from "@xyflow/react";
import "@xyflow/react/dist/style.css";
import dagre from "dagre";
import {
  GitBranch,
  RefreshCw,
  Loader2,
  RotateCcw,
  Code,
  Clock,
  Hash,
} from "lucide-react";
import { fetchVersions } from "@/lib/api";
import type { Version } from "@/lib/types";

// Custom node for versions (DSL expressions)
function VersionNode({ data }: { data: Record<string, unknown> }) {
  const version = data as unknown as Version & { isRoot?: boolean; isLatest?: boolean };
  const expression = version.expression;

  // Truncate long expressions
  const displayExpr = expression.length > 40
    ? expression.slice(0, 37) + "..."
    : expression;

  return (
    <div
      className={`px-4 py-3 border-2 rounded-lg min-w-[180px] max-w-[280px] text-left shadow-md transition-all ${
        version.isLatest
          ? "bg-primary/30 border-primary ring-2 ring-primary/50"
          : version.isRoot
            ? "bg-amber-500/20 border-amber-500"
            : "bg-card border-border hover:border-primary/50"
      }`}
    >
      <Handle type="target" position={Position.Top} className="!bg-primary !w-3 !h-3" />
      <div className="flex items-start gap-2">
        <Code className={`w-4 h-4 mt-0.5 flex-shrink-0 ${
          version.isLatest ? "text-primary" : version.isRoot ? "text-amber-500" : "text-muted-foreground"
        }`} />
        <div className="flex-1 min-w-0">
          <code className="text-xs font-mono break-all leading-relaxed">
            {displayExpr}
          </code>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div className="flex items-center gap-2 mt-2 text-xs text-muted-foreground">
        <Clock className="w-3 h-3" />
        <span>{formatTime(version.created_at)}</span>
      </div>
      {version.isLatest && (
        <div className="mt-1 text-xs text-primary font-medium">Latest</div>
      )}
      {version.isRoot && !version.isLatest && (
        <div className="mt-1 text-xs text-amber-500 font-medium">Root</div>
      )}
      <Handle type="source" position={Position.Bottom} className="!bg-primary !w-3 !h-3" />
    </div>
  );
}

function formatTime(isoString: string): string {
  try {
    const date = new Date(isoString);
    return date.toLocaleTimeString(undefined, {
      hour: '2-digit',
      minute: '2-digit',
      second: '2-digit'
    });
  } catch {
    return isoString;
  }
}

const nodeTypes = {
  version: VersionNode,
};

// Node dimensions
const NODE_WIDTH = 220;
const NODE_HEIGHT = 80;

// Layout algorithm using dagre for proper graph layout
function layoutVersionGraph(
  versions: Version[]
): { nodes: Node[]; edges: Edge[] } {
  if (versions.length === 0) {
    return { nodes: [], edges: [] };
  }

  // Create a new dagre graph
  const dagreGraph = new dagre.graphlib.Graph();
  dagreGraph.setDefaultEdgeLabel(() => ({}));

  // Configure the layout - top to bottom for version history
  dagreGraph.setGraph({
    rankdir: "TB", // Top to bottom (chronological)
    nodesep: 60,   // Horizontal spacing between nodes
    ranksep: 80,   // Vertical spacing between ranks
    marginx: 40,
    marginy: 40,
    ranker: "network-simplex",
  });

  // Find root nodes (no parent) and latest node (most recent)
  const rootIds = new Set<string>();
  const childIds = new Set<string>();

  versions.forEach((v) => {
    if (v.parent_id === null) {
      rootIds.add(v.id);
    } else {
      childIds.add(v.id);
    }
  });

  // Find latest (most recent by created_at)
  const sortedByDate = [...versions].sort(
    (a, b) => new Date(b.created_at).getTime() - new Date(a.created_at).getTime()
  );
  const latestId = sortedByDate[0]?.id;

  // Add nodes to the dagre graph
  versions.forEach((version) => {
    dagreGraph.setNode(version.id, {
      width: NODE_WIDTH,
      height: NODE_HEIGHT,
    });
  });

  // Add edges (parent -> child)
  versions.forEach((version) => {
    if (version.parent_id) {
      dagreGraph.setEdge(version.parent_id, version.id);
    }
  });

  // Run the layout algorithm
  dagre.layout(dagreGraph);

  // Extract positions from dagre and create React Flow nodes
  const layoutedNodes: Node[] = versions.map((version) => {
    const dagreNode = dagreGraph.node(version.id);
    return {
      id: version.id,
      type: "version",
      position: {
        x: dagreNode.x - NODE_WIDTH / 2,
        y: dagreNode.y - NODE_HEIGHT / 2,
      },
      data: {
        ...version,
        isRoot: rootIds.has(version.id),
        isLatest: version.id === latestId,
      } as Record<string, unknown>,
    };
  });

  // Create edges with styling
  const layoutedEdges: Edge[] = versions
    .filter((v) => v.parent_id)
    .map((v) => ({
      id: `${v.parent_id}->${v.id}`,
      source: v.parent_id!,
      target: v.id,
      type: "smoothstep",
      animated: false,
      style: {
        stroke: "#6366f1", // indigo
        strokeWidth: 2,
      },
      markerEnd: {
        type: MarkerType.ArrowClosed,
        color: "#6366f1",
      },
    }));

  return { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges };
}

interface VersionDAGProps {
  /** Increment this to trigger a refresh */
  refreshTrigger?: number;
}

export function VersionDAG({ refreshTrigger = 0 }: VersionDAGProps) {
  const [versions, setVersions] = useState<Version[]>([]);
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true);
  const [selectedVersion, setSelectedVersion] = useState<Version | null>(null);
  const [nodes, setNodes, onNodesChange] = useNodesState<Node>([]);
  const [edges, setEdges, onEdgesChange] = useEdgesState<Edge>([]);

  // Load versions and apply layout
  const loadVersions = useCallback(async () => {
    setLoading(true);
    const data = await fetchVersions();
    setVersions(data.versions);

    if (data.versions.length > 0) {
      const { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges } = layoutVersionGraph(
        data.versions
      );
      setNodes(layoutedNodes);
      setEdges(layoutedEdges);
    }

    setLoading(false);
  }, [setNodes, setEdges]);

  // Reset layout without refetching data
  const resetLayout = useCallback(() => {
    if (versions.length > 0) {
      const { nodes: layoutedNodes, edges: layoutedEdges } = layoutVersionGraph(
        versions
      );
      setNodes(layoutedNodes);
      setEdges(layoutedEdges);
    }
  }, [versions, setNodes, setEdges]);

  useEffect(() => {
    loadVersions();
  }, [loadVersions]);

  // Auto-refresh when trigger changes
  useEffect(() => {
    if (refreshTrigger > 0) {
      loadVersions();
    }
  }, [refreshTrigger]); // eslint-disable-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps

  const onNodeClick = useCallback(
    (_: React.MouseEvent, node: Node) => {
      const version = versions.find((v) => v.id === node.id);
      setSelectedVersion(version || null);
    },
    [versions]
  );

  // Count unique expressions and branches
  const stats = useMemo(() => {
    const uniqueExprs = new Set(versions.map(v => v.expression_hash)).size;
    const roots = versions.filter(v => v.parent_id === null).length;
    return { total: versions.length, uniqueExprs, roots };
  }, [versions]);

  if (loading && versions.length === 0) {
    return (
      <div className="flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-full gap-4 text-muted-foreground">
        <Loader2 className="w-8 h-8 animate-spin" />
        <p>Loading version history...</p>
      </div>
    );
  }

  if (versions.length === 0) {
    return (
      <div className="flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-full gap-4 text-muted-foreground p-6">
        <GitBranch className="w-16 h-16" />
        <h2 className="text-xl font-medium text-foreground">Version History</h2>
        <p className="text-center max-w-md">
          No version history available. Run some DSL expressions to see the version DAG.
        </p>
        <button
          onClick={loadVersions}
          className="flex items-center gap-2 px-4 py-2 bg-primary text-primary-foreground rounded hover:bg-primary/90"
        >
          <RefreshCw className="w-4 h-4" />
          Refresh
        </button>
      </div>
    );
  }

  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col h-full">
      {/* Header */}
      <div className="flex items-center justify-between p-4 border-b border-border">
        <div className="flex items-center gap-4">
          <h2 className="text-lg font-semibold flex items-center gap-2">
            <GitBranch className="w-5 h-5" />
            Version History
          </h2>
          <div className="flex items-center gap-3 text-sm text-muted-foreground">
            <span>{stats.total} versions</span>
            <span>&middot;</span>
            <span>{stats.uniqueExprs} unique expressions</span>
          </div>
        </div>
        <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
          <button
            onClick={resetLayout}
            className="flex items-center gap-2 px-3 py-1.5 text-sm border border-border rounded hover:bg-accent"
            title="Reset node positions"
          >
            <RotateCcw className="w-4 h-4" />
            Reset
          </button>
          <button
            onClick={loadVersions}
            disabled={loading}
            className="flex items-center gap-2 px-3 py-1.5 text-sm border border-border rounded hover:bg-accent disabled:opacity-50"
            title="Reload data"
          >
            <RefreshCw className={`w-4 h-4 ${loading ? "animate-spin" : ""}`} />
            Reload
          </button>
        </div>
      </div>

      {/* Graph */}
      <div className="flex-1 relative">
        <ReactFlow
          nodes={nodes}
          edges={edges}
          onNodesChange={onNodesChange}
          onEdgesChange={onEdgesChange}
          onNodeClick={onNodeClick}
          nodeTypes={nodeTypes}
          fitView
          fitViewOptions={{ padding: 0.3 }}
          minZoom={0.1}
          maxZoom={2}
          className="bg-background"
        >
          <Background color="#374151" gap={20} />
          <Controls
            showInteractive={false}
            className="!bg-card !border-border !shadow-lg"
          />
          <MiniMap
            nodeColor={(node) => {
              const data = node.data as Record<string, unknown>;
              if (data?.isLatest) return "#6366f1";
              if (data?.isRoot) return "#f59e0b";
              return "#6b7280";
            }}
            maskColor="rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.7)"
            className="!bg-card !border-border"
          />
        </ReactFlow>

        {/* Legend */}
        <div className="absolute bottom-4 left-4 bg-card border border-border rounded-lg p-3 text-xs space-y-2">
          <div className="font-medium mb-2">Legend</div>
          <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
            <div className="w-4 h-3 bg-primary/30 border-2 border-primary rounded" />
            <span>Latest version</span>
          </div>
          <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
            <div className="w-4 h-3 bg-amber-500/20 border-2 border-amber-500 rounded" />
            <span>Root (no parent)</span>
          </div>
          <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
            <div className="w-4 h-3 bg-card border-2 border-border rounded" />
            <span>Intermediate version</span>
          </div>
        </div>

        {/* Version details panel */}
        {selectedVersion && (
          <div className="absolute top-4 right-4 w-80 bg-card border border-border rounded-lg p-4 shadow-lg max-h-[80%] overflow-y-auto">
            <div className="flex items-center justify-between mb-3">
              <h3 className="font-medium flex items-center gap-2">
                <Code className="w-4 h-4 text-primary" />
                Version Details
              </h3>
              <button
                onClick={() => setSelectedVersion(null)}
                className="text-muted-foreground hover:text-foreground"
              >
                &times;
              </button>
            </div>

            <div className="space-y-3 text-sm">
              <div>
                <span className="text-muted-foreground block mb-1">Expression:</span>
                <code className="block p-2 bg-secondary/50 rounded text-xs font-mono break-all">
                  {selectedVersion.expression}
                </code>
              </div>

              <div className="grid grid-cols-2 gap-2">
                <div>
                  <span className="text-muted-foreground block">Created:</span>
                  <span>{new Date(selectedVersion.created_at).toLocaleString()}</span>
                </div>
                <div>
                  <span className="text-muted-foreground block">Parent:</span>
                  <span className="font-mono text-xs">
                    {selectedVersion.parent_id
                      ? selectedVersion.parent_id.slice(0, 8) + "..."
                      : "None (root)"}
                  </span>
                </div>
              </div>

              <div>
                <span className="text-muted-foreground flex items-center gap-1 mb-1">
                  <Hash className="w-3 h-3" />
                  Expression Hash:
                </span>
                <code className="block p-2 bg-secondary/50 rounded text-xs font-mono break-all">
                  {selectedVersion.expression_hash}
                </code>
              </div>

              <div>
                <span className="text-muted-foreground block mb-1">Version ID:</span>
                <code className="block p-2 bg-secondary/50 rounded text-xs font-mono">
                  {selectedVersion.id}
                </code>
              </div>

              {selectedVersion.message && (
                <div>
                  <span className="text-muted-foreground block mb-1">Message:</span>
                  <p className="p-2 bg-secondary/50 rounded text-xs">
                    {selectedVersion.message}
                  </p>
                </div>
              )}
            </div>
          </div>
        )}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

There's a TypeScript error. Inside the if (viewMode === "dag") block, TypeScript has narrowed the type of viewMode to "dag", so it thinks the comparison to "list" is always false. I need to adjust the code to not do this comparison inside the block.


Looking at the code, in the DAG view branch I have buttons that check viewMode === "list" and viewMode === "dag" for styling, but inside the if (viewMode === "dag") block, TypeScript knows viewMode is "dag" so the comparison is always false for "list".

## Next Steps (Recommended Priority)

### Option A: Complete Incremental Execution (High Impact) â­ RECOMMENDED
**Why**: Currently we detect cached prefixes but still re-execute everything. True incremental eval would:
- Load cached intermediate outputs into ExecutionContext
- Only execute the uncached suffix of the pipeline
- Provide significant speedup for iterative analysis

**Implementation**:
1. Modify `eval_handler` to load cached outputs when prefix found
2. Update evaluator to accept pre-populated context
3. Build suffix expression from uncached steps
4. Execute only the suffix

### Option B: Dynamic Slots (Technical Debt)
**Why**: The fixed `DataSlot` enum (27 types) limits flexibility. String-based slots would:
- Allow user-defined slot names in DSL
- Remove barrier to adding new data types
- Enable more natural data flow

**Implementation**:
1. Replace `DataSlot` enum with `String` slot identifiers
2. Update ExecutionContext to use HashMap<String, Value>
3. Update primitives to declare slots in TOML specs
4. Migrate existing code

### Option C: Cross-Session Queries (Phase 9 Preview)
**Why**: Enable searching across all sessions for patterns and insights:
- "Find all PERMANOVA with p < 0.05"
- "Show sessions using beta_diversity with bray_curtis"
- Foundation for LLM-powered synergy detection

**Implementation**:
1. Add `GET /search` endpoint with query parameters
2. Index expressions, results, and metadata
3. Return matching versions across sessions

### Option D: Publication Support (Phase 11 Preview)
**Why**: Generate reproducible research outputs:
- Auto-generate methods section from provenance graph
- Export publication-quality figures
- Create reproducibility package

**Implementation**:
1. Add `GET /export/methods` endpoint
2. Template-based prose generation from graph
3. Figure export with proper DPI/format options

     1â†’# Phase 4: Semantic Caching for DSL Expressions
     2â†’
     3â†’## Summary
     4â†’
     5â†’Add pipeline-level caching to the DSL evaluator so that repeated expressions with identical inputs skip re-evaluation and return cached results instantly.
     6â†’
     7â†’## Current State
     8â†’
     9â†’**Already implemented (primitive-level):**
    10â†’- `executor.rs` checks cache before executing YAML commands
    11â†’- `find_cached_node(operation, input_hash)` in storage.rs
    12â†’- Content-based hashing of inputs (primitive + params + file contents)
    13â†’- Cache status shown in briefing
    14â†’
    15â†’**Missing (expression-level):**
    16â†’- `POST /eval` doesn't check for cached expressions before evaluation
    17â†’- No pipeline-level caching (evaluate longest cached prefix)
    18â†’
    19â†’## Design Decisions
    20â†’
    21â†’| Decision | Choice | Rationale |
    22â†’|----------|--------|-----------|
    23â†’| Cache scope | Expression + inputs | Same expression with same data should return cached result |
    24â†’| Cache key | SHA256(expression + input_file_hashes) | Content-addressable |
    25â†’| Cache location | Provenance DB (versions + artifacts) | Already tracks expressions |
    26â†’| MVP scope | Full expression caching | Partial pipeline caching is future enhancement |
    27â†’
    28â†’## Implementation Approach
    29â†’
    30â†’### Cache Key Computation
    31â†’
    32â†’```rust
    33â†’fn compute_expression_cache_key(
    34â†’    expression: &str,
    35â†’    input_files: &[String],
    36â†’    data_dir: &Path,
    37â†’) -> String {
    38â†’    // Hash: expression_normalized + sorted(input_file_content_hashes)
    39â†’    let mut hasher = ContentHasher::new();
    40â†’    hasher.update(expression.as_bytes());
    41â†’
    42â†’    // Sort and hash input file contents
    43â†’    for file in sorted(input_files) {
    44â†’        if let Ok(hash) = ContentHasher::hash_file(data_dir.join(file)) {
    45â†’            hasher.update(hash.as_bytes());
    46â†’        }
    47â†’    }
    48â†’
    49â†’    hasher.finalize().to_string()
    50â†’}
    51â†’```
    52â†’
    53â†’### Cache Lookup Flow
    54â†’
    55â†’```
    56â†’POST /eval "counts |> filter(0.1) |> tmm()"
    57â†’    â”‚
    58â†’    â”œâ”€â–º Parse & typecheck

    60â†’    â”œâ”€â–º Load session data (track input_files)

    62â†’    â”œâ”€â–º Compute cache_key = hash(expression + input_file_hashes)
    63â†’    â”‚
    64â†’    â”œâ”€â–º Lookup: SELECT * FROM versions WHERE cache_key = ?
    65â†’    â”‚       â”‚
    66â†’    â”‚       â”œâ”€â–º Cache HIT:
    67â†’    â”‚       â”‚       â€¢ Get version's output artifacts
    68â†’    â”‚       â”‚       â€¢ Verify output files exist with matching hashes

The entire pipeline is always executed.\n\n### 2. **Prefix Detection Implementation in `provenance.rs`**\n\n#### `find_longest_cached_prefix()` (lines 394-427)\n\n```rust\npub fn find_longest_cached_prefix(\n    &self,\n    steps: &[bioforge::dsl::PipelineStep<'_>],\n    input_files: &[String],\n    data_dir: &Path,\n) -> Result<Option<(usize, String, Version)>>\n```\n\n**What it does:**\n1. Iterates through pipeline steps from longest to shortest prefix (excluding full expression)\n2. For each prefix (0 to len-2):\n   - Builds prefix expression string by serializing steps\n   - Computes cache key via `compute_expression_cache_key()`\n   - Checks if cached via `find_cached_expression(&prefix_key)`\n   - Returns immediately on first match: `(step_index, cache_key, Version)`\n\n**Returns:**\n- `Some((last_cached_step_index, cache_key, version))` if a prefix is cached\n- `None` if no prefix is cached\n\n#### `cache_pipeline_prefixes()` (lines 429-476)\n\nCalled AFTER successful full evaluation to store cache keys for future incremental runs.\n\n```rust\npub fn cache_pipeline_prefixes(\n    &self,\n    steps: &[bioforge::dsl::PipelineStep<'_>],\n    input_files: &[String],\n    data_dir: &Path,\n    parent_id: Option<&VersionId>,\n) -> Result<()>\n```\n\n**What it does:**\n1. Only caches prefixes (0 to len-2), NOT the full expression\n2. For each prefix:\n   - Serializes steps into expression string\n   - Computes cache key using `compute_expression_cache_key()`\n   - Checks if already cached (skips if duplicate)\n   - Creates a Version record for that prefix with cache_key\n\n**Key Design**: Each prefix becomes a separate Version entry in SQLite, enabling incremental re-runs.\n\n### 3. **Cache Key Computation**\n\n#### `compute_expression_cache_key()` (provenance.rs:480-513)\n\n```\ncache_key = SHA256(\n    expression_text +\n    \":\" +\n    sorted(for each input file:\n        filename + \"=\" + file_content_hash + \",\"\n    )\n)\n```\n\n**Deterministic factors:**\n- Normalized expression text\n- Sorted input file names (order-independent)\n- SHA256 hash of each input file's actual content\n- Result is stable across sessions if expression and inputs unchanged\n\n### 4. **Output Artifacts Available for Cached Versions**\n\nWhen a version is cached, the system stores:\n\n**In SQLite (ProvenanceGraph):**\n- `Version` table: expression, expression_hash, cache_key, parent_id, created_at\n- `Node` table: input_hash, output_hash, duration_ms\n- `Artifact` table: node_id, slot, content_hash, filename\n- `Edge` table: source node â†’ target node data flow\n\n**In Filesystem:**\n- All output data files saved by `save_eval_outputs()`:\n  - `filtered_counts.csv`, `normalized_counts.csv`, `transformed_counts.csv`\n  - `p_values.json`, `ordination.json`, `distance_matrix.csv`\n  - Any other populated slots (lines 1021-1043)\n\n**Available for incremental skipping:**\n- Last cached step index tells us which output slot to use as input\n- Output filename can be reconstructed from DataSlot enum\n- File exists check confirms data availability\n\n### 5. **Response Format with Caching Info** (lines 883-887)\n\n```json\n{\n  \"pipeline\": {\n    \"steps_total\": 4,\n    \"steps_cached\": 2,\n    \"steps_executed\": 2\n  },\n  \"provenance\": {\n    \"inputs\": [\"counts.csv\", \"metadata.csv\"],\n    \"outputs\": [\"filtered_counts.csv\", \"normalized_counts.csv\", \"transformed_counts.csv\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 6. **PipelineStep Structure** (pipeline.rs:24-54)\n\n```rust\npub enum PipelineStep<'a> {\n    Source(&'a Expr),           // Initial data source\n    Call {\n        call: &'a Call,         // Function call details\n        span: Span,             // Position info\n    },\n}\n\nimpl PipelineStep {\n    pub fn serialize(&self) -> String { ... }  // For cache key\n    pub fn name(&self) -> Option<&str> { ... } // Get function name\n}\n```\n\n### 7. **Where We Could Skip Execution**\n\nFor incremental evaluation to work, we need to:\n\n1. **After `find_longest_cached_prefix()` finds a match:**\n   - Identify the last cached step index (e.g., step 1 = \"filter\")\n   - Find output slot name for step 1 (e.g., \"FilteredCounts\")\n   - Load that cached output file into ExecutionContext\n\n2. **Modify the evaluator to support suffix-only eval:**\n   - Skip steps 0 to N where N = last_cached_step_index\n   - Start evaluation from step N+1\n   - Use cached output as input to step N+1\n\n3. **Load cached outputs before suffix evaluation:**\n   ```rust\n   if let Some((cached_idx, _, _)) = &cached_prefix {\n       let output_slot = step_to_output_slot(steps[*cached_idx]);\n       load_cached_output(&mut evaluator, output_slot, &data_dir);\n   }\n   // Then evaluate steps[cached_idx+1..]\n   ```\n\n4. **Keep execution plan that tracks step skipping:**\n   - Current: always evaluates steps 0 to N\n   - Target: conditionally evaluate steps M to N based on cached_idx\n\n### 8. **Current Limitations**\n\n- **No lazy evaluation**: Even with cache hits detected, the entire pipeline runs\n- **No step-level execution**: Evaluator doesn't support \"start from step N\"\n- **No output loading before evaluation**: Can't reuse cached outputs as starting points\n- **Response reports hypothetical savings**: `steps_cached` shows potential but isn't used\n\n### 9. **Type System Support** (pipeline.rs:169-209)\n\n```rust\npub struct CachedPrefix {\n    pub last_cached_step: Option<usize>,\n    pub cache_key: Option<String>,\n    pub cached_output: Option<String>,\n}\n```\n\nThis structure exists in the codebase but isn't used in the current eval_handler flow. It could be leveraged for incremental evaluation if the evaluator was modified to support suffix-only runs.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n**Current state**: Prefix caching is **detected and reported** but **not acted upon**. The system:\n- Finds longest cached prefixes correctly\n- Reports steps_cached accurately  \n- Still executes everything anyway\n- Stores prefix cache keys for future runs\n\n**To enable incremental eval**, you need to:\n1. Modify `Evaluator::eval()` to accept a starting step index\n2. Load cached outputs before starting suffix evaluation\n3. Skip Source step and jump to step N+1\n4. Use the cached output as initial state\n\nThe infrastructure and data availability are all in placeâ€”it's just a matter of implementing the suffix-only execution path."

Let me create a detailed analysis document:\n\n## Exploration Summary: DSL Evaluator and Cached Resumption\n\nBased on my thorough exploration of the BioStack DSL evaluator and pipeline system, here's a comprehensive analysis of how to implement resumption from cached intermediate states:\n\n---\n\n## 1. How the DSL Evaluator Works\n\n### 1.1 Core Evaluation Flow (`bioforge/src/dsl/eval.rs`)\n\nThe `Evaluator` struct orchestrates DSL expression execution:\n\n```rust\npub struct Evaluator<'a> {\n    registry: &'a PrimitiveRegistry,        // Function lookup\n    context: ExecutionContext,              // Data flow container\n    variables: HashMap<String, Value>,      // Variable bindings\n    work_dir: Option<std::path::PathBuf>,   // File path resolution\n}\n```\n\n**Key Methods:**\n- `eval(&mut self, expr: &Expr) -> DslResult<Value>` - Entry point\n- `eval_expr(&mut self, expr: &Expr)` - Recursive expression evaluation\n- `eval_call(&mut self, call: &Call, piped: Option<Value>)` - Primitive execution\n- `load_slot()` / `save_slot()` - Persistent I/O for data slots\n\n**Pipe Handling (lines 176-181):**\n```rust\nExprKind::Pipe(left, call) => {\n    let left_value = self.eval_expr(left)?;           // Evaluate source\n    self.eval_call(call, Some(left_value), expr.span) // Pass as implicit arg\n}\n```\n\nThe pipe operator is syntactic sugar that evaluates the left side, then passes the result to the right side's function call.\n\n### 1.2 Execution Context (`bioforge/src/primitive/context.rs`)\n\nThe `ExecutionContext` maintains **all stateful data** during evaluation:\n\n```rust\npub struct ExecutionContext {\n    data: HashMap<DataSlot, Box<dyn Any + Send + Sync>>,  // Typed data storage\n    params: HashMap<String, ParamValue>,                   // Step parameters\n    feature_ids: Vec<FeatureId>,                           // Maintained across steps\n    sample_ids: Vec<SampleId>,                             // Maintained across steps\n    groups: Option<Vec<String>>,                           // Optional grouping\n    provenance_callback: Option<Box<...>>,                 // For recording history\n}\n```\n\n**Critical capabilities:**\n- `set<T>()` / `get<T>()` - Type-safe data access via `DataSlot` keys\n- `set_param()` / `param_or()` - Parameter management\n- `load_slot()` / `save_slot()` - Persistence via `SlotPersistence` trait\n- `save_all_slots()` - Snapshot entire state to a directory\n\n**Data Slots** (29 variants defined in `requirements.rs`):\n- `Counts`, `FilteredCounts`, `NormalizedCounts`, `TransformedCounts`\n- `PValues`, `AdjustedPValues`, `LogFoldChanges`, `TestStatistics`\n- `DistanceMatrix`, `OrdinationResult`, `AlphaDiversity`, `BetaDiversity`\n- etc.\n\nEach slot has a **canonical filename** (e.g., `normalized_counts.csv`), enabling automatic I/O discovery.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Pipeline Decomposition (`bioforge/src/dsl/pipeline.rs`)\n\n### 2.1 Flattening Expressions\n\n`flatten_pipeline(expr: &Expr) -> Vec<PipelineStep>` extracts the sequence of operations:\n\n```rust\npub enum PipelineStep<'a> {\n    Source(&'a Expr),                     // Initial data source\n    Call { call: &'a Call, span: Span }   // Function call in pipeline\n}\n\nfn collect_pipeline_steps<'a>(expr: &'a Expr, steps: &mut Vec<PipelineStep<'a>>) {\n    match &expr.node {\n        ExprKind::Pipe(left, call) => {\n            collect_pipeline_steps(left, steps);    // Recursively process left\n            steps.push(PipelineStep::Call { ... }); // Add this call\n        }\n        _ => steps.push(PipelineStep::Source(expr)) // Base case\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Example:**\n```\nExpression:  counts |> filter(0.1) |> tmm() |> beta_diversity(\"bray_curtis\")\nFlattens to:\n  [0] Source(counts)\n  [1] Call(filter)\n  [2] Call(tmm)\n  [3] Call(beta_diversity)\n```\n\n### 2.2 Cache Key Computation\n\n`compute_prefix_cache_key(steps: &[PipelineStep], step_index: usize, input_hash: &str) -> String`\n\nCreates a content-addressable key for the prefix `steps[0..=step_index]`:\n\n```rust\nfn compute_prefix_cache_key(...) {\n    let mut hasher = ContentHasher::new();\n    hasher.update(input_hash.as_bytes());      // Original data hash\n    hasher.update(b\":\");\n    \n    for (i, step) in steps.iter().enumerate() {\n        if i > step_index { break; }\n        hasher.update(step.serialize().as_bytes()); // Each step's canonical form\n        hasher.update(b\"|\");\n    }\n    \n    hasher.finalize().to_string()  // Deterministic SHA-256\n}\n```\n\n**Determinism:** Same expression + input = same cache key (enables perfect hit detection)\n\n### 2.3 Prefix Matching Result\n\n```rust\npub struct CachedPrefix {\n    pub last_cached_step: Option<usize>,    // Index of last cached step\n    pub cache_key: Option<String>,          // The computed key\n    pub cached_output: Option<String>,      // SlotRef or data path\n}\n\nimpl CachedPrefix {\n    pub fn steps_to_skip(&self) -> usize {\n        self.last_cached_step.map(|i| i + 1).unwrap_or(0)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. How Resumption Could Work\n\n### 3.1 Architecture for Cached Resumption\n\n```\nâ”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”\nâ”‚ Evaluator with Cached Resumption                             â”‚\nâ”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 1. Flatten to pipeline steps                                 â”‚\nâ”‚    [Source(counts), Call(filter), Call(tmm), Call(permanova)]â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 3. Compute prefix cache keys                                 â”‚\nâ”‚    Key[0] = hash(input + \"counts\")                           â”‚\nâ”‚    Key[1] = hash(input + \"counts\" + \"filter(0.1)\")          â”‚\nâ”‚    Key[2] = hash(input + \"counts\" + \"filter(0.1)\" + \"tmm\")  â”‚\nâ”‚    Key[3] = hash(input + ... + \"permanova(...)\")            â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 4. Probe cache (longest match first)                         â”‚\nâ”‚    Lookup Key[3] â†’ MISS                                      â”‚\nâ”‚    Lookup Key[2] â†’ HIT! cached_output = NormalizedCounts    â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 5. Build suffix expression (uncached steps)                  â”‚\nâ”‚    remaining = [Call(permanova)]                             â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 6. Load cached state                                         â”‚\nâ”‚    ctx.load_slot(NormalizedCounts, path)                     â”‚\nâ”‚    ctx.set_feature_ids(...)                                  â”‚\nâ”‚    ctx.set_sample_ids(...)                                   â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 7. Evaluate suffix only                                      â”‚\nâ”‚    eval_call(permanova, ...) â†’ result                        â”‚\nâ”‚                                                               â”‚\nâ”‚ 8. Store and return                                          â”‚\nâ”‚    ctx.save_slot(...)                                        â”‚\nâ”‚    Return result                                             â”‚\nâ””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜\n```\n\n### 3.2 Key Changes Required\n\n#### A. Evaluator Enhancement\n\nAdd a cached resumption path:\n\n```rust\nimpl<'a> Evaluator<'a> {\n    /// Evaluate with automatic cache resumption\n    pub fn eval_cached(\n        &mut self,\n        expr: &Expr,\n        cache_lookup: impl Fn(&str) -> Option<CacheEntry>,\n        input_hash: &str,\n    ) -> DslResult<Value> {\n        // Step 1: Flatten and analyze\n        let steps = flatten_pipeline(expr);\n        \n        // Step 2: Find longest cached prefix\n        for i in (0..steps.len()).rev() {\n            let key = compute_prefix_cache_key(&steps, i, input_hash);\n            if let Some(entry) = cache_lookup(&key) {\n                // Found a cache hit!\n                if i == steps.len() - 1 {\n                    // Entire pipeline cached\n                    return load_cached_result(&entry);\n                } else {\n                    // Partial hit - load prefix, evaluate suffix\n                    self.load_cached_state(&entry)?;\n                    return self.eval_suffix(&steps, i + 1);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // No cache hit - evaluate normally\n        self.eval_expr(expr)\n    }\n    \n    /// Evaluate only the remaining uncached steps\n    fn eval_suffix(\n        &mut self,\n        steps: &[PipelineStep],\n        start_index: usize,\n    ) -> DslResult<Value> {\n        let mut result = Value::Unit;\n        \n        for (idx, step) in steps.iter().enumerate() {\n            if idx < start_index { continue; }\n            \n            result = match step {\n                PipelineStep::Source(_) => {\n                    // Already loaded, skip\n                    Value::SlotRef(\"counts\".to_string())\n                }\n                PipelineStep::Call { call, span } => {\n                    self.eval_call(call, Some(result), *span)?\n                }\n            };\n        }\n        \n        Ok(result)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### B. State Loading Mechanism\n\nLoad cached context (slots, IDs, parameters):\n\n```rust\nimpl<'a> Evaluator<'a> {\n    /// Load cached intermediate state\n    fn load_cached_state(&mut self, entry: &CacheEntry) -> Result<()> {\n        // Load the main output slot\n        self.context.load_slot(entry.output_slot, &entry.output_path)?;\n        \n        // Restore IDs if available\n        if let Some(ref feature_ids_path) = entry.feature_ids_path {\n            self.context.load_slot(DataSlot::FeatureIds, feature_ids_path)?;\n        }\n        if let Some(ref sample_ids_path) = entry.sample_ids_path {\n            self.context.load_slot(DataSlot::SampleIds, sample_ids_path)?;\n        }\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### C. Suffix Expression Construction\n\nThe suffix is implicitly represented by the remaining `PipelineStep` values:\n\n```rust\n/// Build a suffix expression from remaining steps\nfn build_suffix_expr(steps: &[PipelineStep], start_idx: usize) -> Option<Expr> {\n    if start_idx >= steps.len() {\n        return None;\n    }\n    \n    // Start with a reference to the cached data\n    let mut expr = match &steps[0] {\n        PipelineStep::Source(e) => (*e).clone(),\n        _ => unreachable!()\n    };\n    \n    // Pipe remaining calls\n    for step in &steps[start_idx..] {\n        if let PipelineStep::Call { call, span } = step {\n            expr = Expr::new(\n                ExprKind::Pipe(Box::new(expr), (*call).clone()),\n                *span\n            );\n        }\n    }\n    \n    Some(expr)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Integration with Content-Addressable Storage\n\n### 4.1 ContentHasher (`bioforge/src/provenance/hasher.rs`)\n\nProvides deterministic SHA-256 hashing:\n\n```rust\npub struct ContentHasher { ... }\n\nimpl ContentHasher {\n    pub fn hash_string(s: &str) -> Hash { ... }\n    pub fn hash_file(path: &Path) -> Result<Hash> { ... }\n    pub fn hash_json(value: &serde_json::Value) -> Hash { ... }\n    pub fn hash_operation(operation: &str, params: &Value) -> Hash { ... }\n}\n```\n\n**For cached resumption:**\n1. Hash the original input file: `hash_file(\"counts.csv\")`\n2. For each step, hash the serialized operation: `hash_operation(\"filter\", params)`\n3. Combine to get cache key: `ContentHasher::combine(&[input_hash, op_hash])`\n\n### 4.2 Cache Storage Schema\n\nFrom `INCREMENTAL_EVALUATION_EXPLORATION.md`, the ideal cache table:\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE evaluation_cache (\n    cache_key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,          -- Deterministic key\n    input_hash TEXT NOT NULL,\n    operation TEXT NOT NULL,             -- \"filter_prevalence\", \"tmm\", etc.\n    params JSONB,\n    \n    output_slot TEXT,                    -- Which DataSlot contains result\n    output_hash TEXT,\n    output_location TEXT,                -- Path to serialized output\n    \n    feature_ids_path TEXT,               -- Restore point: IDs\n    sample_ids_path TEXT,\n    \n    computed_at TIMESTAMP,\n    compute_duration_ms INTEGER,\n    \n    FOREIGN KEY(prefix_hash) REFERENCES pipeline_prefixes(hash)\n);\n\nCREATE TABLE pipeline_prefixes (\n    prefix_hash TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    expression_prefix TEXT,              -- Serialized first N steps\n    step_count INTEGER,\n    output_slot TEXT,\n    output_hash TEXT,\n    first_computed_at TIMESTAMP,\n    compute_count INTEGER\n);\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Data Flow Example: Complete Walkthrough\n\n**Expression:**\n```biostack\ncounts |> filter(0.1) |> normalize(\"tmm\") |> permanova(~ treatment)\n```\n\n**Step-by-step execution with cached resumption:**\n\n| Phase | Action | Cache State |\n|-------|--------|-------------|\n| **Parse & Flatten** | Steps = [Source(counts), Call(filter), Call(tmm), Call(permanova)] | - |\n| **Hash Input** | input_hash = SHA256(\"counts.csv\") = \"abc123...\" | - |\n| **Probe Step 3** | key3 = hash(\"abc123...\\|filter\\|tmm\\|permanova\") | MISS |\n| **Probe Step 2** | key2 = hash(\"abc123...\\|filter\\|tmm\") | **HIT!** cached_output_slot = NormalizedCounts, cached_path = \"cache/blobs/norm_123.parquet\" |\n| **Load Cached** | ctx.load_slot(NormalizedCounts, \"norm_123.parquet\"); ctx.load_slot(FeatureIds, \"feat_ids.txt\"); ctx.load_slot(SampleIds, \"samp_ids.txt\") | Context restored to post-TMM state |\n| **Evaluate Suffix** | Suffix = [Call(permanova)]; eval_call(permanova, ...) | Only PERMANOVA computed (~15s instead of ~2s) |\n| **Store Result** | ctx.save_slot(PValues, \"out/pvalues.json\") | New cache entries for key3 created |\n\n**Performance Impact:**\n- Without cache: Load(1s) + Filter(0.5s) + TMM(0.5s) + PERMANOVA(15s) = **17s**\n- With cache: Load(1s) + [Hit] + PERMANOVA(15s) = **16s** (not much savings in this case)\n- But if running 10 variations of PERMANOVA on same data: 16s + 9Ã—(0.01s cached) = **16.09s** vs 17Ã—10 = **170s** (10x faster!)\n\n---\n\n## 6. What Needs to Change\n\n### 6.1 Must Implement\n\n1. **Cache Storage Layer**\n   - SQLite/PostgreSQL backend with tables from schema above\n   - `lookup_cached_prefix(key: &str) -> Option<CacheEntry>`\n   - `store_cache_entry(entry: CacheEntry)`\n\n2. **Enhanced Evaluator**\n   - `eval_cached()` method with cache probe logic\n   - `load_cached_state()` to restore context\n   - `eval_suffix()` to evaluate remaining steps\n\n3. **Slot Metadata Persistence**\n   - When saving cached results, also save feature/sample IDs\n   - `CacheEntry` must track which DataSlot is the main output\n\n### 6.2 Nice to Have\n\n1. **Speculative Evaluation** - Pre-compute likely next steps while waiting\n2. **Parallel Branching** - Evaluate multiple suffixes in parallel from same prefix\n3. **Cache Statistics** - Track hit rates, compute time saved, space used\n4. **Provenance Integration** - Mark nodes as \"cached\" vs \"computed\"\n5. **Cross-Session Sharing** - Lab-wide cache for common computations\n\n### 6.3 Minimal MVP\n\nFor a working MVP, you only need:\n\n1. A `HashMap<String, (DataSlot, PathBuf)>` in memory cache (or simple SQLite)\n2. Modify `Evaluator` to:\n   - Flatten the pipeline\n   - Compute cache keys\n   - Check if cached before evaluating\n   - Load and resume if hit\n3. Enhanced `ExecutionContext` to save/restore IDs alongside data\n\n---\n\n## 7. Key Insights\n\n1. **Pipes are sequential, not nested** - `flatten_pipeline()` gives you the execution order. Resumption at any point is straightforward.\n\n2. **DataSlots are the currency** - Everything flows through `ExecutionContext` with typed data in named slots. Cache entries just save/restore these.\n\n3. **Content addressing is deterministic** - Same expression + input always gives same key. No cache invalidation logic needed!\n\n4. **IDs must be preserved** - When resuming, feature/sample IDs must travel with the data. The context maintains them, so restore them too.\n\n5. **Suffix evaluation reuses the normal evaluator** - No special evaluator needed for suffix. Just set the context state and `eval_call()` the remaining steps.\n\n6. **The pipeline.rs module is designed for this** - `flatten_pipeline()` and `compute_prefix_cache_key()` are already there, waiting to be used in a resumption layer.\n\nThis exploration shows that the architecture is **already well-positioned** for cached resumption - the building blocks exist, they just need to be connected with a cache backend and resumption logic in the evaluator."

Current State:
1. eval_handler already detects cached prefixes via find_longest_cached_prefix()
2. It reports steps_cached in the response
3. But it still executes the ENTIRE pipeline (there's a TODO comment about this)
4. The infrastructure is all there - we just need to connect it


What needs to happen:
1. When a cached prefix is found, load the cached outputs into the ExecutionContext
2. Build a suffix expression (or just evaluate the remaining steps)
3. Skip the source loading and cached steps
4. Only execute the uncached suffix


The key insight is that the evaluator handles pipes by:
1. Evaluating the left side
2. Passing the result to the right side's function call


So for resumption, we need to:
1. Load the cached output into the context
2. Get a Value representing that output (likely Value::SlotRef)
3. Pass that value through the remaining calls


Let me now design the implementation plan and write it to the plan file.

     1â†’//! Pipeline analysis for incremental evaluation.
     2â†’//!
     3â†’//! This module provides utilities for analyzing pipe expressions to enable
     4â†’//! incremental evaluation with prefix caching.
     5â†’//!
     6â†’//! ## Example
     7â†’//!
     8â†’//! ```ignore
     9â†’//! use bioforge::dsl::{parse, pipeline::flatten_pipeline};
    10â†’//!
    11â†’//! let expr = parse("counts |> filter(0.1) |> tmm()")?;
    12â†’//! let steps = flatten_pipeline(&expr);
    13â†’//!
    14â†’//! // steps = [
    15â†’//! //   PipelineStep::Source("counts"),
    16â†’//! //   PipelineStep::Call { name: "filter", ... },
    17â†’//! //   PipelineStep::Call { name: "tmm", ... },
    18â†’//! // ]
    19â†’//! ```
    20â†’
    21â†’use crate::dsl::ast::{Arg, Call, Expr, ExprKind, Literal, Span};
    22â†’use crate::provenance::ContentHasher;
    23â†’
    24â†’/// A step in a pipeline expression.
    25â†’#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    26â†’pub enum PipelineStep<'a> {
    27â†’    /// The source expression (first element before any pipes)
    28â†’    Source(&'a Expr),
    29â†’    /// A function call in the pipeline
    30â†’    Call {
    31â†’        /// The call AST node
    32â†’        call: &'a Call,
    33â†’        /// The span of the entire pipe expression up to this point
    34â†’        span: Span,
    35â†’    },
    36â†’}
    37â†’
    38â†’impl<'a> PipelineStep<'a> {
    39â†’    /// Get the function name if this is a Call step.
    40â†’    pub fn name(&self) -> Option<&str> {
    41â†’        match self {
    42â†’            PipelineStep::Source(_) => None,
    43â†’            PipelineStep::Call { call, .. } => Some(&call.name.node),
    44â†’        }
    45â†’    }
    46â†’
    47â†’    /// Serialize this step for cache key computation.
    48â†’    pub fn serialize(&self) -> String {
    49â†’        match self {
    50â†’            PipelineStep::Source(expr) => serialize_expr(expr),
    51â†’            PipelineStep::Call { call, .. } => serialize_call(call),
    52â†’        }
    53â†’    }
    54â†’}
    55â†’
    56â†’/// Flatten a pipeline expression into a sequence of steps.
    57â†’///
    58â†’/// The returned steps are in execution order: source first, then each
    59â†’/// piped function call.
    60â†’///
    61â†’/// For non-pipeline expressions, returns a single Source step.
    62â†’pub fn flatten_pipeline(expr: &Expr) -> Vec<PipelineStep<'_>> {
    63â†’    let mut steps = Vec::new();
    64â†’    collect_pipeline_steps(expr, &mut steps);
    65â†’    steps
    66â†’}
    67â†’
    68â†’/// Recursively collect pipeline steps from left to right.
    69â†’fn collect_pipeline_steps<'a>(expr: &'a Expr, steps: &mut Vec<PipelineStep<'a>>) {
    70â†’    match &expr.node {
    71â†’        ExprKind::Pipe(left, call) => {
    72â†’            // First collect from the left side
    73â†’            collect_pipeline_steps(left, steps);
    74â†’            // Then add this call
    75â†’            steps.push(PipelineStep::Call {
    76â†’                call,
    77â†’                span: expr.span,
    78â†’            });
    79â†’        }
    80â†’        ExprKind::Paren(inner) => {
    81â†’            // Unwrap parentheses
    82â†’            collect_pipeline_steps(inner, steps);
    83â†’        }
    84â†’        _ => {
    85â†’            // Base case: non-pipe expression is the source
    86â†’            steps.push(PipelineStep::Source(expr));
    87â†’        }
    88â†’    }
    89â†’}
    90â†’
    91â†’/// Compute a cache key for a pipeline prefix.
    92â†’///
    93â†’/// The prefix includes steps 0..=step_index.
    94â†’///
    95â†’/// # Arguments
    96â†’///
    97â†’/// * `steps` - The full pipeline steps
    98â†’/// * `step_index` - The index of the last step to include in the prefix
    99â†’/// * `input_hash` - Hash of the input data (file contents)
   100â†’///
   101â†’/// # Returns
   102â†’///
   103â†’/// A content-addressable cache key.
   104â†’pub fn compute_prefix_cache_key(
   105â†’    steps: &[PipelineStep<'_>],
   106â†’    step_index: usize,
   107â†’    input_hash: &str,
   108â†’) -> String {
   109â†’    let mut hasher = ContentHasher::new();
   110â†’
   111â†’    // Include input hash
   112â†’    hasher.update(input_hash.as_bytes());
   113â†’    hasher.update(b":");
   114â†’
   115â†’    // Include each step up to and including step_index
   116â†’    for (i, step) in steps.iter().enumerate() {
   117â†’        if i > step_index {
   118â†’            break;
   119â†’        }
   120â†’        let serialized = step.serialize();
   121â†’        hasher.update(serialized.as_bytes());
   122â†’        hasher.update(b"|");
   123â†’    }
   124â†’
   125â†’    hasher.finalize().to_string()
   126â†’}
   127â†’
   128â†’/// Serialize an expression to a canonical string for hashing.
   129â†’fn serialize_expr(expr: &Expr) -> String {
   130â†’    match &expr.node {
   131â†’        ExprKind::Ident(name) => name.clone(),
   132â†’        ExprKind::Literal(lit) => serialize_literal(lit),
   133â†’        ExprKind::List(items) => {
   134â†’            let items_str: Vec<_> = items.iter().map(serialize_expr).collect();
   135â†’            format!("[{}]", items_str.join(","))
   136â†’        }
   137â†’        ExprKind::Call(call) => serialize_call(call),
   138â†’        ExprKind::Pipe(left, call) => {
   139â†’            format!("{}|>{}", serialize_expr(left), serialize_call(call))
   140â†’        }
   141â†’        ExprKind::Paren(inner) => format!("({})", serialize_expr(inner)),
   142â†’    }
   143â†’}
   144â†’
   145â†’/// Serialize a literal to a canonical string.
   146â†’fn serialize_literal(lit: &Literal) -> String {
   147â†’    match lit {
   148â†’        Literal::Integer(i) => format!("{}", i),
   149â†’        Literal::Float(f) => format!("{}", f),
   150â†’        Literal::String(s) => format!("\"{}\"", s),
   151â†’        Literal::Boolean(b) => format!("{}", b),
   152â†’    }
   153â†’}
   154â†’
   155â†’/// Serialize a call to a canonical string.
   156â†’fn serialize_call(call: &Call) -> String {
   157â†’    let args_str: Vec<_> = call.args.iter().map(serialize_arg).collect();
   158â†’    format!("{}({})", call.name.node, args_str.join(","))
   159â†’}
   160â†’
   161â†’/// Serialize an argument to a canonical string.
   162â†’fn serialize_arg(arg: &Arg) -> String {
   163â†’    match arg {
   164â†’        Arg::Positional(expr) => serialize_expr(expr),
   165â†’        Arg::Named { name, value } => format!("{}:{}", name, serialize_expr(value)),
   166â†’    }
   167â†’}
   168â†’
   169â†’/// Result of finding the longest cached prefix.
   170â†’#[derive(Debug)]
   171â†’pub struct CachedPrefix {
   172â†’    /// Index of the last cached step (0-based).
   173â†’    /// None if no steps are cached.
   174â†’    pub last_cached_step: Option<usize>,
   175â†’    /// Cache key of the longest cached prefix.
   176â†’    pub cache_key: Option<String>,
   177â†’    /// The output slot or value from the cached prefix.
   178â†’    pub cached_output: Option<String>,
   179â†’}
   180â†’
   181â†’impl CachedPrefix {
   182â†’    /// No cached prefix found.
   183â†’    pub fn none() -> Self {
   184â†’        Self {
   185â†’            last_cached_step: None,
   186â†’            cache_key: None,
   187â†’            cached_output: None,
   188â†’        }
   189â†’    }
   190â†’
   191â†’    /// A cached prefix was found.
   192â†’    pub fn found(step_index: usize, cache_key: String, output: String) -> Self {
   193â†’        Self {
   194â†’            last_cached_step: Some(step_index),
   195â†’            cache_key: Some(cache_key),
   196â†’            cached_output: Some(output),
   197â†’        }
   198â†’    }
   199â†’
   200â†’    /// Check if any prefix is cached.
   201â†’    pub fn has_cache(&self) -> bool {
   202â†’        self.last_cached_step.is_some()
   203â†’    }
   204â†’
   205â†’    /// Get the number of steps that can be skipped.
   206â†’    pub fn steps_to_skip(&self) -> usize {
   207â†’        self.last_cached_step.map(|i| i + 1).unwrap_or(0)
   208â†’    }
   209â†’}
